  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ac281333-a92c-47f5-980b-d65431e583c3'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14748396339603979240">Socrates in Love took the Japanese publishing industry by storm, becoming the all-time best selling novel in Japan! Finally, U.S. readers will be able to experience the phenomenon that became the inspiration for a blockbuster movie, a hit TV show, and a popular manga. A national sensation that touched over three million readers, Kyoichi Katayama brought innocent love and r</span>
  <span id="freeText14748396339603979240" style="display:none">Socrates in Love took the Japanese publishing industry by storm, becoming the all-time best selling novel in Japan! Finally, U.S. readers will be able to experience the phenomenon that became the inspiration for a blockbuster movie, a hit TV show, and a popular manga. A national sensation that touched over three million readers, Kyoichi Katayama brought innocent love and romance to the forefront of Japan's ultra-hip mass market. Affectionately known as "Sekachu" in Japan, Katayama's novel depects a sweet high school romance between an average guy and a popular girl. But tragedy ensues when the girl falls ill with leukemia. A bittersweet tale of young love, enduring devotion, and heartbreaking loss, socrates in Love is a story to cherish and nurture.</span>

    <a title="Greta G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45248887-greta-g"><img alt="Greta G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525435609p2/45248887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1365243666?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greta G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greta G" href="/user/show/45248887-greta-g">Greta G</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781421513928" href="/book/show/3215824-socrates-in-love">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365243666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10567050254564927219"><b>Love is a form of violence that forces you to think.</b><br/><br/>There is not much to think about in living for oneself alone. Seeing only oneself is equivalent to seeing nothing. Only through love for someone outside of ourselves do we start thinking about the world and the meaning of true love, life and death. <br/><br/><i>"There's nothing in the world that can be thought through completely. Even if you think you've exhausted a subject, after a while you start feeling you haven't. And then you can think about it some m</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10567050254564927219" style="display:none"><b>Love is a form of violence that forces you to think.</b><br /><br />There is not much to think about in living for oneself alone. Seeing only oneself is equivalent to seeing nothing. Only through love for someone outside of ourselves do we start thinking about the world and the meaning of true love, life and death. <br /><br /><i>"There's nothing in the world that can be thought through completely. Even if you think you've exhausted a subject, after a while you start feeling you haven't. And then you can think about it some more. Eventually, your thoughts gain a reality."</i><br /><br /><i>"There are things that come true in life, and things that don't. The things that actually happen, people forget about right away. But the things that never come true stay in our hearts forever. I'm talking about the things called dreams and longings. I think it's our feelings for these that sustain the beauty of life. All the things that didn't happen have come true, as beauty."</i><br /><br /><i>"My heart refused comprehension. If I took it in, I would fall apart. Like a frozen flower petal given a snap of the fingers, my heart would shatter to pieces."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10567050254564927219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2209063111" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209063111" />
    <a title="Virginia Cavanillas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19380470-virginia-cavanillas"><img alt="Virginia Cavanillas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556819327p2/19380470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209063111?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Cavanillas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Cavanillas" href="/user/show/19380470-virginia-cavanillas">Virginia Cavanillas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19380470-virginia-cavanillas?shelf=rambles">rambles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19380470-virginia-cavanillas?shelf=paperback">paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209063111" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14028754827042646947"><b>Maybe 2.5 bacause all the tears shed deserves at least one star and a half.</b><br/><br/><b>Grey.</b> That’s the color that defines this book to me, and my mood after reading it. Grey. Not the oranges and reds I was expecting. Not even the feared black darkening it all. Just grey. And that, let me tell you, it’s pure disappointment. *sighs in frustration*<br/><br/>The most important highlight about my reading it’s that <b>I was crying from page two</b>. TWO!!!!! Yes, I’m a softie but still... <br/>The thing is that I was a mess at the en</span>
  <span id="freeText14028754827042646947" style="display:none"><b>Maybe 2.5 bacause all the tears shed deserves at least one star and a half.</b><br><br><b>Grey.</b> That’s the color that defines this book to me, and my mood after reading it. Grey. Not the oranges and reds I was expecting. Not even the feared black darkening it all. Just grey. And that, let me tell you, it’s pure disappointment. *sighs in frustration*<br><br>The most important highlight about my reading it’s that <b>I was crying from page two</b>. TWO!!!!! Yes, I’m a softie but still... <br>The thing is that I was a mess at the end and with tears as big as a lake, but I was mad too, <b>I was madder than sad</b> because those big tears didn’t come from the feelz the story was inspiring me. No. I was crying just because a girl’s death makes me cry. It’s sad and awful and I hate cancer with all I have, and here the unfairness is huge. But the crying came from that fact and that fact only. I was sad for the event itself, not because what I was reading was beautiful or precious because I didn’t feel it that way. It was... ok, I guess. <br>Do I have any sense? This is the worst of my ramblings *sighs again with obvious frustration* (more evident that the sighs in the first paragraph)<br><br>The dying thing is not a spoiler, don’t you worry. That’s what you’re going to read if you choose this novel. The protagonist’s death is told in the first page (first sentence maybe?) and that’s what this book is about: <b>two kids falling in love while one of them is dying</b>. But this is not a romance novel, maybe we could consider it YA because of the age of both when this story starts, but I wouldn’t know how to call or classify this book since I don’t see it as a love story, because if it was, it failed spectacularly with me. <br>This is a tale of little things, moments and situations lived between our protagonist during the short time they have together. <br>Some philosophical stuff here and there and a few instants with a depth I didn’t feel. This was not what I was looking for and it bored me a bit (between tear and tear)<br><br>To my Spanish friends: In Spain the tittle is completely different if you want to try the translated version. It’s called <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4655733.Un_grito_de_amor_desde_el_centro_del_mundo" title="Un grito de amor desde el centro del mundo by Kyōichi Katayama" rel="nofollow noopener">Un grito de amor desde el centro del mundo</a> and it was published on paperback a few years ago (2008?)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512836098i/24637608._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> So, if you are in the mood for a teenage drama, a sweet tragedy, read it. Because you can’t trust my opinion in here since I can’t even explain why it didn’t work for me. Maybe it’s full of feels and I just didn’t get to them, or they didn’t get to me, or whatever. And it’s an irony since I was crying and sobbing like a little girl.<br><br>This book has inspired a comic, a TV series in Japan and a movie... so, I guess it has been magical for a lot of people and I’m the weird one who was expecting more and I didn’t found that something to blow my mind. What I find is a lot of tears that got my hubby begging me to quit, a lot of “<i>I don’t care about that, move on and tell me other kind of things”</i> and a lot of sighing. Sadly, I didn’t love the story but maybe I could try the manga, because they are so cute and there’s a possibility this way I can feel more between them. Does it sound superficial? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512836098i/24637609.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, if you’re attracted to the blurb, give it a go and don’t mind me, who knows, maybe for you is a hit!<br><br><a href="https://reviewsforbooklovers.blogspot.com.es/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reviews for Book Lovers</a><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503517262ra/23670232.gif" width="100" height="90" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14028754827042646947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2592742732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2592742732" />
    <a title="Raquel Baggins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60099374-raquel-baggins"><img alt="Raquel Baggins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601211766p2/60099374.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2592742732?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Raquel Baggins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Raquel Baggins" href="/user/show/60099374-raquel-baggins">Raquel Baggins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9788466323567" href="/book/show/9077889-un-grito-de-amor-desde-el-centro-del-mundo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=asian-lit">asian-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60099374-raquel-baggins?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2592742732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15225998396904940934"><blockquote>
  <i>«(…) desde que nací, no ha habido un solo segundo en que tú no hayas estado en este mundo.»</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Review in English | Reseña en español (abajo)</b><br/><i>Socrates in Love</i> is a tender and beautiful story, but it hasn’t touched me. I felt a sort of 'it’s not you, it’s me’ because I know that if I’d read it when I was a teenager (14 or 15 years old), I would have enjoyed it a lot more. It’s a story of love and loss among teenagers with very pure feelings, and there are extremely wonderful dialogues -especially b</span>
  <span id="freeText15225998396904940934" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>«(…) desde que nací, no ha habido un solo segundo en que tú no hayas estado en este mundo.»</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Review in English | Reseña en español (abajo)</b><br /><i>Socrates in Love</i> is a tender and beautiful story, but it hasn’t touched me. I felt a sort of 'it’s not you, it’s me’ because I know that if I’d read it when I was a teenager (14 or 15 years old), I would have enjoyed it a lot more. It’s a story of love and loss among teenagers with very pure feelings, and there are extremely wonderful dialogues -especially between Sakutarô and his grandfather-. From the beginning we know how it's going to end –it’s not something that bothered me, tho– but I haven’t managed to connect with these characters or being invested in the story at any time. Maybe I've already passed that time in which you think that if you lose a loved one you won’t be able to live without them; or maybe I've become practical over the years. The parts that I liked the most are those that make more references to mourning and loss in a general way, and in which philosophical (and moral) questions are raised about the loss of an important person in your life. Thus, I was invested because I irremediably remembered my grandma’s death. If it were been the story of, by example, some parents facing the death of their daughter, I know that I’d have been touched and got emotional; but in the end, it’s a teenage story that I found little credible.<br /><br />All in all, I’d recommend it if you like tender love stories or if you want to give a try to one of the most famous novels of recent times in Japan.<br /><br /><b>P. S. I'm not English, so if you see any mistakes let me know so I can correct them, please</b><br />—<br />Es una historia tierna y un libro bonito, pero no me ha llegado a emocionar. Sé que si lo hubiese leído siendo adolescente (con 14-15 años), lo hubiese disfrutado muchísimo porque es una historia de amor y pérdida entre adolescentes con sentimientos muy puros, y hay diálogos maravillosos –especialmente entre Sakutarô y su abuelo–. Desde el inicio de la historia sabemos cómo va a terminar –no es algo que me haya molestado, la verdad–, pero no he llegado a conectar con estos personajes en ningún momento. Quizás ya he pasado esa época en la que piensas que si pierdes a un ser querido no vas a ser capaz de rehacer tu vida; o quizás me he vuelto práctica con los años. Las partes que me han gustado son las que hacen mayor referencia al duelo y la pérdida de forma general, y donde se plantean cuestiones de tipo filosófico (y moral) sobre la pérdida de una persona importante en tu vida. Ahí sí conecté porque me acordé irremediablemente de mi abuela. Si fuera la visión de, por ejemplo, unos padres frente a la muerte de su hija, sé que hubiese conectado más con la historia; pero no deja de ser una historia adolescente que me ha parecido poco creíble.<br /><br />Con todo, os la recomendaría si os gustan las historias tiernas de amor o si os apetece darle una oportunidad a una de las novelas más famosas de los últimos tiempos en Japón.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15225998396904940934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8643254055266711878" style="display:none">4/5stars<br /><br />I LOVED THIS. LIKE WOW.<br /><br />Okay so I binge read this in 1 day obviously, and I loved it. <br /><br />We follow "Saku-chan" who is a teenage boy, in love with his best friend since childhood, Aki. You know from the very beginning that Aki has recently died. The author then takes you through their life together, from the moment the two met, up until Aki's passing. This story was beautiful, and extremely relateable on a lot of aspects. It brought up a lot of great conversations too such as faith (is there a heaven? is there god? what comes after death?), what does love mean, and several other great points. It was slightly cliche, sure, but it did those "cliche" things a lot better than any novels I've read!</span>

<div id="review_264222882" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264222882" />
    <a title="trang" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6166468-trang"><img alt="trang" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581943560p2/6166468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264222882?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="trang" class="user" itemprop="url" name="trang" href="/user/show/6166468-trang">trang</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12082965-ti-ng-g-i-t-nh-y-u-gi-a-l-ng-th-gi-i">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6166468-trang?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6166468-trang?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6166468-trang?shelf=japanese-literature">japanese-literature</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264222882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14749497022013530945">Long enough to be a well-told story, yet short enough for readers not to fall asleep. I intentionally took the book from my roommate's bookshelf as a type of sleeping pill when the computer was not available, keeping in mind the idea that "this is gonna another stupid love story". I even kept calling it "Socrates in Hell" as my personal habit of sarcasm for love tends to grow years after years.<br/><br/>The book turned out to be great! In terms of small details, Katayama's story telling is unbelievable, c</span>
  <span id="freeText14749497022013530945" style="display:none">Long enough to be a well-told story, yet short enough for readers not to fall asleep. I intentionally took the book from my roommate's bookshelf as a type of sleeping pill when the computer was not available, keeping in mind the idea that "this is gonna another stupid love story". I even kept calling it "Socrates in Hell" as my personal habit of sarcasm for love tends to grow years after years.<br /><br />The book turned out to be great! In terms of small details, Katayama's story telling is unbelievable, considering his age when writing about teenagers. Don't be fooled by the word "teenagers', because you'll find love at its true meaning and at its purest level. Personally, I've got fed up with sex getting in the way of almost every story and film or animated movie recently (not that it is of unimportance, but they put too much stress into physical contact). By "unbelievable", I mean the author created exceptionally good characters. Matsumoto Sakutaro and his grandfather: A youngster that has a large part of an old man, and an old man whose heart is of a youngster in the spring. Sakutaro's dialogue or monologue was always the part I like the most about "Socrates in love". Romanticism never fails to confirm its root in most of our readers, Katayama Kyoichi once again proves that.<br /><br />My general impression of the book is that it suits to be the content of a typical anime, from the scenic background of the story (the temple, the beach, the street, the sunset, etc. very much Japan!) to the art of story telling, especially how the two main characters are perfect for each other. I heard "Socrates in Love" was adapted into movie and manga and will definitely take a look over those versions.<br /><br />My words have certainly failed to describe the essence of its beauty because of the limitation of verbal words themselves and the limitation of my own personal ability to express. But you should check it out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14749497022013530945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2306065237164801680">I didn't really know what to expect when I borrowed this from the library as I missed the hype the first time round when the book was published 15 years ago, and the blurb is a bit opaque... so at the risk of repeating the obvious let me say this: it's a tearjerker of a love story about high school lovers, one of whom dies of a nasty disease. This is not a spoiler, by the way, we know this within a page or two of the first chapter. What makes it compelling is the development of the love between </span>
  <span id="freeText2306065237164801680" style="display:none">I didn't really know what to expect when I borrowed this from the library as I missed the hype the first time round when the book was published 15 years ago, and the blurb is a bit opaque... so at the risk of repeating the obvious let me say this: it's a tearjerker of a love story about high school lovers, one of whom dies of a nasty disease. This is not a spoiler, by the way, we know this within a page or two of the first chapter. What makes it compelling is the development of the love between the two against such a tragic end. It's the wreck on the highway that we just can't help slowing down for as we pass, just to see what it was all about and piece together a narrative that makes sense of young love, life and death. Reminiscent of Haruki Murakami's Norwegian Wood, but dare I say it, better. Moving, compelling and lingers long after the last page.<br /><br />Download my starter library for free here - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://eepurl.com/bFkt0X">http://eepurl.com/bFkt0X</a> - and receive my monthly newsletter with book recommendations galore for the Japanophile/crime fiction/English-as-a-foreign-language teacher in all of us.</span>

<div id="review_203189669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203189669" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6146409-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314513209p2/6146409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203189669?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/6146409-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203189669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11376959082519605804">In the novel Socrates in Love, an average boy named Sakutaro Matsumoto meets a girl who changes his life forever. As they get to know one another, they began to discover feelings like no other. Their relationship was perfect; he loved her and she loved him. When life couldn’t get any better, it got worse, Aki was diagnose with leukemia. Now, in a world without Aki, Saku struggles to let go as he lingers in the past, trapped in his own beloved memory of Aki.<br/><br/>The theme of this novel is, “lingering </span>
  <span id="freeText11376959082519605804" style="display:none">In the novel Socrates in Love, an average boy named Sakutaro Matsumoto meets a girl who changes his life forever. As they get to know one another, they began to discover feelings like no other. Their relationship was perfect; he loved her and she loved him. When life couldn’t get any better, it got worse, Aki was diagnose with leukemia. Now, in a world without Aki, Saku struggles to let go as he lingers in the past, trapped in his own beloved memory of Aki.<br /><br />The theme of this novel is, “lingering in the past will only make it difficult to move on, therefore it is better to let go and keep it as a memory.” In the book, Saku couldn’t bring himself to forget about Aki or to ever live a life without her. In this passage, Saku flashbacks to the time when he was on the train to Australia with Aki; he thought to himself, “I don’t know where the past had gone, why the present was so painful. I couldn’t believe such a pain was real.” (pg. 128-129) This passage supports my theme because it speaks about how the past can be so painful and unforgettable that it becomes unbearable. Saku’s painful past affected his life tremendously and unfortunately led him to live a life full of misery and sorrow. Saku continues to linger in the past and falls deeper into his loving memory of Aki. <br /><br />In this passage, said by Saku’s grandfather, he says, “No, I don’t think the person I love will ever appear in front of me again in the same form I knew before. But she and I have always been together. These last fifty years, there never was one moment when we weren’t together.”(147)This passage support the second part of my theme because it tells us that Saku’s grandfather was able to let go, leave her as a memory, and live life to the fullest even though she was no longer here. In this part, Saku’s grandfather is trying to bring Saku back to reality to start living life again. In this passage Saku says,” I took a small glass jar from my jacket pocket. I had intended to carry on me for the rest of my life-but surely I didn’t need to do that. In this world, there are beginnings and ending. Aki was both. I had the feeling this was enough.” (pg. 168) This shows that Saku was able to learn what was best for him, to finally let Aki go and leave her as a memory.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11376959082519605804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3299738655" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3299738655" />
    <a title="Brendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13730311-brendy"><img alt="Brendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460428420p2/13730311.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brendy" href="/user/show/13730311-brendy">Brendy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/4655733-un-grito-de-amor-desde-el-centro-del-mundo">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3299738655" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1189290754715723579"><div>
  <br/>
  <a href='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1438168630l/4655733._SY475_.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img height='640' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1438168630l/4655733._SY475_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <br/>
</div><br/><div>
<br/>Where do I start? I've read this book two times, both in spanish so I decided that I'd also tagged its name in spanish just as its exactly translation from spanish to english, because-not sure why- its translation to english they changed the title for Socrates in love-not quite sure about it, I believe it's cause the manga-</div><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <a href='https://image.myanimelist.net/ui/BQM6jEZ-UJLgGUuvrNkYUCG8p-X1WhZLiR4h-oxkqQeBRBDdkdOjQt6eDACqauhK_uWlQZkz0hJ_uRHJydU63Q' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img height='179' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587847036ra/29357332.gif' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <br/>
</div><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <br/>
</div><br/><div>
  <br/>
  <br/>
</div><br/><div>
<br/>This book came to me in a really strange way, I was looking for something to read and out of nowhere I read the nam</div></span>
  <span id="freeText1189290754715723579" style="display:none"><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1438168630l/4655733._SY475_.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="640" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1438168630l/4655733._SY475_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>Where do I start? I've read this book two times, both in spanish so I decided that I'd also tagged its name in spanish just as its exactly translation from spanish to english, because-not sure why- its translation to english they changed the title for Socrates in love-not quite sure about it, I believe it's cause the manga-</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://image.myanimelist.net/ui/BQM6jEZ-UJLgGUuvrNkYUCG8p-X1WhZLiR4h-oxkqQeBRBDdkdOjQt6eDACqauhK_uWlQZkz0hJ_uRHJydU63Q" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587847036ra/29357332.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>This book came to me in a really strange way, I was looking for something to read and out of nowhere I read the name, which reminded me to an anime I watched in my high school time, an anime that everysingle time I watched it-and were more than two, because I bought the DVDs-made me cry and made me feel that real love was actually something real, no matter how difficult the world could be or how hard everyone can make you think it would be. The anime was <b>Saikano, </b>which in spanish they added to the name the phrase: <i>"The last love song in this little planet"</i>, and as you, my dear reader may realise, both phrases are quite similar-I mean to the book's title, of course- so thinking that maybe the manga was based on this book, I bought without even doubting-because come on! the manga was so damn good, that later was published the anime, the ova and the live action movie, so why would I think there was not possible to get a book as well , right ?</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/proxy/AFw7rk2B1su6BbdgsmFgRvUuvycSzEMi603B2PlusLe-ChwjMQcRiB822nxyFaCfaad8ebejnSsjk8t24yXEAbxZssTpQnB6Nr9WdV8wCDDGV51xzJd0" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="300" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587847036i/29357333.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>But great was my surprise when the principal character weren't even named like the anime-way more when there was no war or machines either, yeah I didn't even read the synopsis-but still I wasn't depressed I was just more curious, and kept reading, besides I bought it in spanish and was quite easier to read it, because the pace was pretty relaxed so I went on... <b>and couldn't be more happier of doing so.</b>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <b>
    <br>
  </b>
</div><br><div>
<br>This book tells us the story of Aki Hirose and Sakutaro Matsumoto, both school partners know each other since kids, and making their friendship growing to a beautiful and sincere love.</div><br><div>
<br>Like a "slice of life-anime" we can read in 3 parts of the book-because is divided in 4- how the love between both of them was flourishing, how they met, their behaviour at school, at their parents, their families and such - because they were still being kids- so if you have ever watched an anime you can realise what I mean when I say it was like a slice of life-anime-yeah they tell you of how it was being delegate, how were their dates, their weekends and of course, how they tried to have sex for first time-and if to that you add rural japanese scenaries and sweet anecdotes of their relatives of how the live used to be, you will be teletransported to an innocent, relaxed and lovely panorama right away, giving to the reader a way of peace.</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>But not everything is as good as it looks like, here comes the part of drama: <b>Aki gets sick, </b>changing the genere of the book completely from romance to drama-a heartbreaking, sobbing kind of drama- one of those where you say: "nahhh, I'm okay; I can handle it", but then you find yourself blinking away the tears from your eyes because they don't let you keep reading-yup that kind of drama-</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-_PQs9YTI_os/XqSWhhUnOGI/AAAAAAAAUOg/QmBqA7wfH5s4aq39ZZi3qiJz6oPirPpKQCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/sa1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="400" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587847036i/29357336.jpg" width="290" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>The first time I read it, I cried an ocean...but the second one I just shed a few tears -guess because I already knew what was coming-but still the story is worth it.</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jrw0v0PYWzA/XqSYVc0ttAI/AAAAAAAAUOs/4A27ACFUGfM89uAd0FR4SDEFYL4fbgypACLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/sa2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="286" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587847036i/29357335.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>The book shows us different types of love, but all of them pure in their own especial way and also how to handle the lost of a beloved one. Here I had to name Saku's grandpa, I think he's the wise man from the book, giving you the best stories that will make you say: <b>WOW, </b>he's the one that will take Saku's hand just in the moments he needs it more.</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-A2tAsr4zvGE/XqSeLchfCSI/AAAAAAAAUPU/EuTEdpnGwtMF2nwhbdxPSw-gAjf_Ru6ZwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/sa5.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="628" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587847036i/29357334._SX540_.jpg" width="640" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>Reading the book the first time was like if someone was getting a hand inside of me and crushing my heart, but the second one was like if someone were hugging me; in both ocassions the book made me realise the kinf of love I want in life and I want to teach to my future family and share with the rest of the world and miss the tranquility of how it was being kid and the sensations of peace and ease you felt in that time.</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>I can´t say more of this book without risking of giving you spoilers, just telling you that is worth the hour and a half of your time-or maybe less, cause it's 200 pages- and if you read it from top to bottom in once...the emotions will be really strong. </div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-5r2exS1uW0g/XqSaYvWMnqI/AAAAAAAAUO8/O_rmCMQqNyEDcfweAZLWIaSJOs9CBR3YwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/sa3.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">

</div><br><div>
  <br>
  <br>
</div><br><div>
<br>May not be Romeo &amp; Juliet or the sweetest and most dramatic love story of the world, but it is a freaking sweet and sad love story.</div><br><div>

<div id="review_1477403683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1477403683" />
    <a title="Juno Tisno" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12011656-juno-tisno"><img alt="Juno Tisno" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460717477p2/12011656.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1477403683?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juno Tisno" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juno Tisno" href="/user/show/12011656-juno-tisno">Juno Tisno</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12011656-juno-tisno?shelf=japan-themed-or-tastes-so">japan-themed-or-tastes-so</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1477403683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12135482609951656355">This books, in my opinion, might be the precedent of modern realistic YA fict. In fact, I can say this book is the Japanese counterpart of Green's The Fault is in Our Star. A sick, yet optimistic girl? Check. A wish to visit other country? Check. A boyfriend who tries his hard to make the wish come true? Check. A philosophical and existential conversation performed by two teenagers? Check, check, check.<br/><br/>Kitayama's writing itself is inarguably enjoyable (I read the translated version, though). It </span>
  <span id="freeText12135482609951656355" style="display:none">This books, in my opinion, might be the precedent of modern realistic YA fict. In fact, I can say this book is the Japanese counterpart of Green's The Fault is in Our Star. A sick, yet optimistic girl? Check. A wish to visit other country? Check. A boyfriend who tries his hard to make the wish come true? Check. A philosophical and existential conversation performed by two teenagers? Check, check, check.<br /><br />Kitayama's writing itself is inarguably enjoyable (I read the translated version, though). It is crafted well, and both the narration and dialogue are written well. Especially the dialogue. I definitely love the conversation about afterlife and society, and their views of the world.<br /><br />Despite its seriousness, this book also contains the very essence of adolescence, hence it can easily be adapted to manga and dorama. For example, Saku's curiousity of sexuality is portrayed well into him tricking Aki to the abandoned hotel in Yumeshima, though in the end, nothing happened. Their needs to be independent is also pictured in their attempt in going to Australia without their parents' consent.<br /><br />Another thing that makes this book good is how prominent the Japanese culture plays in shaping the story. Cremation is one of the Japan's customs in treating the deceased, and it bears a significant role in story. There is also word play about character's name and kanji, which thickens its Japanese aspect<br /><br />To sum up, it is a great book for people searching for meaningful, but not too heavy, young adult fict.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12135482609951656355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer44485746" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4016430145468080002">Katayama Kyoichi's short but charming novel, <i>Socrates In Love</i>, is refreshing look into the sentiment of love, loyalty, and loss, through the eyes of two young high school students.<br/><br/>The main character, Sakutaro or "Saku-chan" and Aki, his girlfriend, are junior high school friends. After they enter high school they begin to realize the mutual feelings they have had for one another, which grow stronger with each new day. They are happy. However, with the sudden and unexpected news of Aki's serious </span>
  <span id="freeText4016430145468080002" style="display:none">Katayama Kyoichi's short but charming novel, <i>Socrates In Love</i>, is refreshing look into the sentiment of love, loyalty, and loss, through the eyes of two young high school students.<br /><br />The main character, Sakutaro or "Saku-chan" and Aki, his girlfriend, are junior high school friends. After they enter high school they begin to realize the mutual feelings they have had for one another, which grow stronger with each new day. They are happy. However, with the sudden and unexpected news of Aki's serious condition, their moments of innocent joy are shattered. She is hospitalized and confined to her room. In one last desperate act of loyalty - and love - Sakutaro sneaks Aki out of the hospital to fly off to "the center of the world," Ayer's Rock Australia. They never make it.<br /><br />Aki believes, in her heart, that death is only an interlude between the first moments of love and love in eternity (which lives on because of its eternal nature.) An interesting afterword concludes this brief and bittersweet tale of beautiful and enduring love. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8107887574926777182">Melissa Wickelhaus<br/>Romance<br/>Socrates in Love follows the story of Sakutaro Matsumoto as he falls in love with his classmate Aki Hirose. Full of innocent love, it’s a typical high school romance until Aki falls ill with leukemia. It is a tale of young love, devotion through difficult times, and loss. The tale is somewhat different from other romances, in that it is told from the male perspective. The characters are well developed, even some of the side characters such as Sakutaro’s grandfather and b</span>
  <span id="freeText8107887574926777182" style="display:none">Melissa Wickelhaus<br />Romance<br />Socrates in Love follows the story of Sakutaro Matsumoto as he falls in love with his classmate Aki Hirose. Full of innocent love, it’s a typical high school romance until Aki falls ill with leukemia. It is a tale of young love, devotion through difficult times, and loss. The tale is somewhat different from other romances, in that it is told from the male perspective. The characters are well developed, even some of the side characters such as Sakutaro’s grandfather and best friend. The images are done in the usual manga style, but are nothing spectacular making this book look like any other average manga. But the story is very sweet and heart wrenching. I would recommend it.<br /></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507499441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17041726623958785168">Well, I read a book in Japanese!<br/><br/>About halfway through this book I thought I was going to give it two stars because it was <em>so</em> predictable and rote. Sakutarō's girlfriend is dead, and we know this because the very first chapter is about the pain he's feeling on the trip to Australia to scatter her ashes. Then it jumps back to how they met, them falling in love and discussing philosophy and what happens after death, the progression of life, until Aki gets leukemia and dies. You know this was coming</span>
  <span id="freeText17041726623958785168" style="display:none">Well, I read a book in Japanese!<br /><br />About halfway through this book I thought I was going to give it two stars because it was <em>so</em> predictable and rote. Sakutarō's girlfriend is dead, and we know this because the very first chapter is about the pain he's feeling on the trip to Australia to scatter her ashes. Then it jumps back to how they met, them falling in love and discussing philosophy and what happens after death, the progression of life, until Aki gets leukemia and dies. You know this was coming because early on, for no reason, Sakutarō calls into a radio station and tells them about his "friend" who was being treated in the hospital and the treatments had made all of her long, beautiful hair fall out, and since she was depressed and alone, he was dedicating <em>West Side Story</em>'s "Tonight" to her.<br /><br />That's what I mean by foreshadowing. The romance was the worst part of this book. <br /><br />There were some bright spots, though. There are very few characters in the book other than Sakutarō and Aki, but the standout was Sakutarō's grandfather, a crotchety wine-drinking, tv-watching old man who was in love with a woman he was never able to marry and still carries a torch for almost fifty years later. He and Sakutarō had some conversations about the afterlife and about death, and about how important experience is and whether anything remains of those you care for after they die, that were the highlight of the book for me.<br /><br />Because really, the book is about how nothing lasts forever and how about things we think are the most important moment of ours lives...aren't. I have, thank G-d, never had a loved one die on me, but I have been a child and I remember how every single setback felt like the end of the world. How everything was the most important moment of my life, and how if I had a falling out with a friend, or did badly on a test, or otherwise came to an inflection point, it meant that everything had changed. But that's not really how it is--life moves on. 物の哀れ <em>mono no aware</em> is the proverb, usually translated as "the transience of things," and it's the reason why cherry blossoms are beautiful. If they were pink all year round, no one would care nearly as much, but it's because they only bloom for two weeks in the spring that people gather under the falling blossoms all day long. Sakutarō and Aki's love was real, and it was strong, but who knows whether it would have lasted. Aki's death is no reason for Sakutarō to just stop. It's like the inverse of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319453702" rel="nofollow noopener">5 Centimeters per Second</a>.<br /><br />While the book was mostly about Sakutarō and Aki, I was barely interested. Once it moves into the way that Sakutarō dealt with Aki's death, though, that's when I sat up and took notice. Two stars at the beginning but the ending was strong enough to raise it to four stars.<br /><br />They should have called it <em>Socrates in Love</em>, like Katayama wanted</span>
  <a data-text-id="17041726623958785168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3089518992" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3089518992" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43522572-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579014398p2/43522572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3089518992?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/43522572-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3089518992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4300069094460625119">I can understand why this book resonated with so many people. It can be interpreted in many different ways depending the reader’s perspective and circumstances. The main story line might be about young love, but it is also about human emotions of loving someone, sacrificing for that person, and dealing with the loss of and longing for that person. It’s also about regrets of missed opportunities and finding ways to reconcile with such regrets. <br/><br/>What would you sacrifice for love? It is true that lo</span>
  <span id="freeText4300069094460625119" style="display:none">I can understand why this book resonated with so many people. It can be interpreted in many different ways depending the reader’s perspective and circumstances. The main story line might be about young love, but it is also about human emotions of loving someone, sacrificing for that person, and dealing with the loss of and longing for that person. It’s also about regrets of missed opportunities and finding ways to reconcile with such regrets. <br /><br />What would you sacrifice for love? It is true that love sometimes is not on a schedule but love without sacrifice is just a word that people say out of convenience. I see two examples in the book that serve as an important reminder that when love hurts, coupled with your willingness to sacrifice for that person, it is when you truly love that person. <br /><br />People often say “Love hurts.”, but from my perspective after reading this book, real love makes you feel better and that love itself shouldn't hurt. Love hurts is when you cannot be with the person you love, but love itself is beautiful, so beautiful that it will make you cry, such as Sakutaro’s love for Aki. <br /><br />Would you consider Sakutaro’s grandfather 50-year longing for his lady friend “love”? Some might consider that act admirable but I differ in opinion; grandfather is a coward when it comes to love because he was not willing to make sacrifices for his lady friend. What if the lady that grandfather said he loved, lived each day with the hope that he will come to take her away but only to be faced with disappointments, day after day for 50 years, until one day she died of a broken heart because she was not worthy enough for him to make sacrifices on her behalf? <br /><br />Grandfather to Sakutaro: "Why is it so painful to lose someone you love? I think it’s because you already love that person. It’s not the parting or their absence itself that’s sad. You love them, and that’s why saying good-bye breaks your heart. That’s why you search for reminders of them and never really stop mourning them. So aren’t grief and mourning nothing more than one facet of your love? Just one expression of the feelings you have for that person?"<br /><br />Grandfather to Sakutaro: "There are things that come true in life, and things that don’t. The things that actually happen, people forget about right away. But the things that never come true stay in our hearts forever. I’m talking about the things called dreams and longings. I think it’s our feelings for these that sustain the beauty of life. All the things that didn’t happen have come true, as beauty."<br /><br />Always.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4300069094460625119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3139043176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3139043176" />
    <a title="Flay Raut" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65121630-flay-raut"><img alt="Flay Raut" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487438102p2/65121630.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3139043176?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flay Raut" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flay Raut" href="/user/show/65121630-flay-raut">Flay Raut</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3139043176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9177376751276006227">"It's very sad when the person you love dies. This grief... it doesn't have shape. No matter what you do. That's why, perhaps, we want to give it shape. Like the poem we just read, it's hard to be parted, but we can be together again."<br/><br/>I misjudged this novel.<br/>I bought this book five (5) years ago in an event as some kind of a personal memorabilia. After that, I abandoned it in my dump of TBR pile.<br/><br/>Fast forward, three (3) years later, I lost my beloved mother. She died of an illness. It was difficul</span>
  <span id="freeText9177376751276006227" style="display:none">"It's very sad when the person you love dies. This grief... it doesn't have shape. No matter what you do. That's why, perhaps, we want to give it shape. Like the poem we just read, it's hard to be parted, but we can be together again."<br /><br />I misjudged this novel.<br />I bought this book five (5) years ago in an event as some kind of a personal memorabilia. After that, I abandoned it in my dump of TBR pile.<br /><br />Fast forward, three (3) years later, I lost my beloved mother. She died of an illness. It was difficult. I suffered a reading slump.. even until now.<br /><br />After a journey of struggling to overcome my grief, putting my life back together, and recovering my enthusiasm for reading and life in general, I constantly switch books 📚 until I came to this one. The first two (2) lines got me:<br /><br />"That morning I woke up crying, as usual. I didn't know anymore whether I was sad or not–my feelings had flowed away with the tears."<br /><br />Hook, line, and sinker.<br />I finished the novel. It was not smooth; I still tend to drop the book aside for days, but that's because I get lost in my thoughts 💭. This book made me think of my grief, the sorrow, the loss, and how I'm "coping" with it. The novel became like a companion for me; Saku was me, Aki was my mother minus the romance, just the love.<br /><br />It is nice to read words that perfectly describes what you go through after the devastating loss of someone you love. It's like the affirmation I've always needed. The affirmation that I couldn't find from others or somewhere else. Everytime I read another line that resonates with me, I was like "Ah, so it was normal. What I went through, what I felt and thought was normal... because someone else also went through it. It's not just me."<br /><br />What grief, sorrow, and loss are, are hard to put into words.<br /><br />Not all can do it, no matter how hard they try. I learned it while talking with people who tried to make me feel better after losing my Mother. None of them could explain to me what was happening, why was it happening, and how. How can I overcome this grief. Or maybe, another possibility, it was me who couldn't grasp what they were saying. <br /><br />That is why this novel is really a blessing for me. Thank you. Thank you, Mr. Kyoichi Katayama..</span>
  <a data-text-id="9177376751276006227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9185434818695162690"><b>Spoiler-free comment </b><br/>Socrates in Love is a simple and beautiful story about life, death, and love. Easy to read and easy to follow, Socrates in Love leads you through the life of a couple of young students who find themselves confronting the harshness of death and questioning what it means to be alive, to be with someone, to love someone, and ultimately to lose someone. <br/><br/>Please give this novel the chance to make you shed some tears. It won't disappoint you.</span>

                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2543804688&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10834841012525830227">I normally hate tragedy, but the tragedy presented at the beginning still urges me so badly to know the story. It's beautiful, and sad at the same time.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ntH9QzNeDhd9MblRTcQYi38KeTs9z9JNjzN6syBCalwMeASCekh1+8Mh64t7HitVuKbbujJy9EHN01+5LwzMrQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NhNSoHWFAQmERAUWZEFzsugpWWcj308BJA0PvJ8ZUf2kuqthPJN65TpUV8xSm0BsL4X75ixiaQ1m7Sq2kFf3DA==')})
  }

Sutil, de finísima y delicada factura,<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9555617938531321445\" style=\"display:none\">Las protagonistas de este singular libro de relatos viven historias de amor. Aunque dispares, se diría que todas ellas están enlazadas, como si fueran partes de un conjunto, a veces armónico, otras menos amable.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/153219.Ky_ichi_Katayama">About Kyōichi Katayama</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/153219.Ky_ichi_Katayama"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1370359139p3/153219.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/153219.Ky_ichi_Katayama">Kyōichi Katayama
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
82
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7895278383160665275">See also <a href='https://www.goodreads.com:443/search/search?q=片山 恭一' title='片山 恭一' rel='noopener'>片山 恭一</a>. Katayama was born in the Ehime Prefecture and graduated from Kyushu University. Katayama's first major book was Kehai (Sign). The book won the Bungakkai Newcomers award.<br/><br/>Katayama wrote the book Socrates in Love (also known as Crying Out Love, In the Center of the World). The book was adapted into a manga (illustrated by Kazumi Kazui), a film, and a Japanese television drama. Socrate</span>
  <span id="freeText7895278383160665275" style="display:none">See also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com:443/search/search?q=片山 恭一" title="片山 恭一" rel="noopener">片山 恭一</a>. Katayama was born in the Ehime Prefecture and graduated from Kyushu University. Katayama's first major book was Kehai (Sign). The book won the Bungakkai Newcomers award.<br /><br />Katayama wrote the book Socrates in Love (also known as Crying Out Love, In the Center of the World). The book was adapted into a manga (illustrated by Kazumi Kazui), a film, and a Japanese television drama. Socrates in Love was his first and, as of 2008, only book translated into English.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7895278383160665275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
